<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Indonesia" title="Names of Indonesia">Names of Indonesia</a></div>
<p>The name <i>Indonesia</i> derives from the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> words <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Indo-" title="wikt:Indo-">Indos</a></i></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">á¼¸Î½Î´ÏÏ</span></span>) and <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%BD%E1%BF%86%CF%83%CE%BF%CF%82" title="wikt:Î½á¿ÏÎ¿Ï">nesos</a></i></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">Î½á¿ÏÎ¿Ï</span></span>), meaning "Indian islands".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EcoSeas1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-EcoSeas1-16">[14]</a></sup> The name dates back to the <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th century</a>, far predating the formation of independent Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indoety_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-indoety-17">[15]</a></sup> In 1850, <a href="/wiki/George_Windsor_Earl" title="George Windsor Earl">George Windsor Earl</a>, an English <a href="/wiki/Ethnology" title="Ethnology">ethnologist</a>, proposed the terms <i>Indunesians</i>âand, his preference, <i>Malayunesians</i>âfor the inhabitants of the "Indian Archipelago or <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEarl1850119_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEarl1850119-18">[16]</a></sup> In the same publication, one of his students, <a href="/wiki/James_Richardson_Logan" title="James Richardson Logan">James Richardson Logan</a>, used <i>Indonesia</i> as a synonym for <i>Indian Archipelago</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEarl1850254,_277â278_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEarl1850254,_277â278-20">[18]</a></sup> Dutch academics writing in East Indies publications were reluctant to use <i>Indonesia</i>. They preferred <i>Malay Archipelago</i> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Maleische Archipel</i>); the <i><a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Netherlands East Indies</a></i> (<span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Nederlandsch Oost IndiÃ«</i></span>), popularly <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">IndiÃ«</i></span>; <i>the East</i> (<span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">de Oost</i></span>); and <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Insulinde</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kroef_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kroef-21">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>After 1900, <i>Indonesia</i> became more common in academic circles outside the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, and native nationalist groups adopted it for political expression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kroef_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kroef-21">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Bastian" title="Adolf Bastian">Adolf Bastian</a> of the University of Berlin popularized the name through his book <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Indonesien oder die Inseln des Malayischen Archipels, 1884â1894</i></span>. The first native scholar to use the name was <a href="/wiki/Ki_Hajar_Dewantara" title="Ki Hajar Dewantara">Ki Hajar Dewantara</a> when in 1913, he established a press bureau in the Netherlands, <span title="Dutch-language text"><i lang="nl">Indonesisch Pers-bureau</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indoety_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-indoety-17">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Indonesia" title="History of Indonesia">History of Indonesia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Borobudur_ship.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="816" data-file-width="1183" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Borobudur_ship.JPG/220px-Borobudur_ship.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Borobudur_ship.JPG/330px-Borobudur_ship.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Borobudur_ship.JPG/440px-Borobudur_ship.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Borobudur_ship.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Borobudur_ship" title="Borobudur ship">Borobudur ship</a> carved on <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> temple, c. 800 CE. Outrigger boats from the archipelago may have made trade voyages to the east coast of Africa as early as the 1st century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Fossilised remains of <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i>, popularly known as the "<a href="/wiki/Java_Man" title="Java Man">Java Man</a>", suggest the Indonesian archipelago was inhabited two million to 500,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> reached the region around 43,000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a>, who form the majority of the modern population, migrated to Southeast Asia from what is now Taiwan. They arrived in the archipelago around 2,000 BCE and confined the native <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesians</a> to the far eastern regions as they spread east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor20035â7_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor20035â7-27">[25]</a></sup> Ideal agricultural conditions and the mastering of <a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">wet-field rice cultivation</a> as early as the eighth century BCE<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor20038â9_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor20038â9-28">[26]</a></sup> allowed villages, towns, and small kingdoms to flourish by the first century CE. The archipelago's strategic sea-lane position fostered inter-island and international trade, including with Indian kingdoms and Chinese dynasties, from several centuries BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor200315â18_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor200315â18-29">[27]</a></sup> Trade has since fundamentally shaped Indonesian history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor20033,_9â11,_13â15,_18â20,_22â23_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor20033,_9â11,_13â15,_18â20,_22â23-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers200518â20,_60,_133â134_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers200518â20,_60,_133â134-31">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the seventh century CE, the <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a> naval kingdom flourished due to trade and the influences of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor200322â26_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor200322â26-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs19913_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs19913-33">[31]</a></sup> Between the eighth and tenth centuries CE, the agricultural Buddhist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sailendra" title="Sailendra">Sailendra</a> and Hindu <a href="/wiki/Mataram_Kingdom" title="Mataram Kingdom">Mataram</a> dynasties thrived and declined in inland Java, leaving grand religious monuments such as Sailendra's <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> and Mataram's <a href="/wiki/Prambanan" title="Prambanan">Prambanan</a>. The Hindu <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> kingdom was founded in eastern Java in the late 13th century, and under <a href="/wiki/Gajah_Mada" title="Gajah Mada">Gajah Mada</a>, its influence stretched over much of present-day Indonesia. This period is often referred to as a "Golden Age" in Indonesian history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Spread_of_Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Spread of Islam in Indonesia">The earliest evidence of Islamized populations</a> in the archipelago dates to the 13th century in northern <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs19913â14_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs19913â14-35">[33]</a></sup> Other parts of the archipelago gradually adopted Islam, and it was the dominant religion in <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and Sumatra by the end of the 16th century. For the most part, Islam overlaid and mixed with existing cultural and religious influences, which shaped the predominant form of Islam in Indonesia, particularly in Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112â14_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112â14-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="6124" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/220px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/330px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg/440px-Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicolaas_Pieneman_-_The_Submission_of_Prince_Dipo_Negoro_to_General_De_Kock.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The submission of <a href="/wiki/Diponegoro" title="Diponegoro">Prince Diponegoro</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Merkus_de_Kock" title="Hendrik Merkus de Kock">General De Kock</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> in 1830.</div></div></div>
<p>The first Europeans arrived in the archipelago in 1512, when Portuguese traders, led by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco SerrÃ£o">Francisco SerrÃ£o</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonialism_in_Indonesia" title="Portuguese colonialism in Indonesia">sought to monopolise</a> the sources of <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cloves" title="Cloves">cloves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Piper_cubeba" title="Piper cubeba">cubeb pepper</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199122â24_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199122â24-37">[35]</a></sup> Dutch and British traders followed. In 1602, the Dutch established the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (VOC) and became the dominant European power for almost 200 years. The VOC was dissolved in 1800 following bankruptcy, and the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Netherlands</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> as a nationalised colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199124_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199124-38">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>For most of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Indonesia#Colonial_era" title="History of Indonesia">colonial period</a>, Dutch control over the archipelago was tenuous. Dutch forces were engaged continuously in quelling rebellions both on and off Java. The influence of local leaders such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Diponegoro" title="Prince Diponegoro">Prince Diponegoro</a> in central Java, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imam_Bonjol" title="Imam Bonjol">Imam Bonjol</a> in central Sumatra, <a href="/wiki/Pattimura" title="Pattimura">Pattimura</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku</a>, and the bloody <a href="/wiki/Aceh_War" title="Aceh War">30-year war in Aceh</a> weakened the Dutch and tied up the colonial military forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchwarz19943â4_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchwarz19943â4-39">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991142_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991142-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage21_21]_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage21_21]-41">[39]</a></sup> Only in the early 20th century did Dutch dominance extend to what was to become Indonesia's current boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage21_21]_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage21_21]-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199161â147_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199161â147-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage209_209â278]_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage209_209â278]-43">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailshistoryofmoderni00adripagen27_10â14]_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailshistoryofmoderni00adripagen27_10â14]-44">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies_campaign" title="Dutch East Indies campaign">Japanese invasion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Japanese occupation of the Dutch East Indies">subsequent occupation</a> during World War II ended Dutch rule<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_45-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-45'>[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> and encouraged the previously suppressed independence movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> Two days after the <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">surrender of Japan</a> in August 1945, <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Hatta" title="Mohammad Hatta">Mohammad Hatta</a>, influential nationalist leaders, <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_Indonesian_Independence" title="Proclamation of Indonesian Independence">proclaimed Indonesian independence</a> and were appointed president and vice-president, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage325_325]_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage325_325]-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bidien1945_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bidien1945-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage325_325]_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesia00jeanpage325_325]-49">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReid197330_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReid197330-52">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Netherlands attempted to re-establish their rule, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">a bitter armed and diplomatic struggle</a> ended in December 1949 when the Dutch formally recognised Indonesian independence in the face of international pressure and transferred sovereignty to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Indonesia" title="United States of Indonesia">United States of Indonesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend200335_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend200335-53">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bidien1945_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bidien1945-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> Despite extraordinary political, social and sectarian divisions, Indonesians, on the whole, found unity in their fight for independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage23_21,_23]_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsindonesiandestin00theopage23_21,_23]-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991211â213_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991211â213-56">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:125px;max-width:125px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:176px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presiden_Sukarno.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4604" data-file-width="3214" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/123px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/185px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Presiden_Sukarno.jpg/246px-Presiden_Sukarno.jpg 2x" width="123"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:123px;max-width:123px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:176px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3582" data-file-width="2455" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg/121px-Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg/182px-Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg/242px-Mohammad_Hatta_1950.jpg 2x" width="121"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Sukarno (<i>left</i>) and Hatta (<i>right</i>), Indonesia's founding fathers and the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">President</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Indonesia" title="Vice President of Indonesia">Vice President</a> respectively.</div></div></div></div>
<p>As president, Sukarno moved Indonesia from democracy towards authoritarianism and maintained power by balancing the opposing forces of <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">the military</a>, political Islam, and the increasingly powerful <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Indonesia" title="Communist Party of Indonesia">Communist Party of Indonesia</a> (PKI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991237â280_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991237â280-57">[55]</a></sup> Tensions between the military and the PKI culminated in <a href="/wiki/30_September_Movement" title="30 September Movement">an attempted coup</a> in 1965. The army, led by Major General <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">Suharto</a>, countered by instigating a <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965â66">violent anti-communist purge</a> that killed between 500,000 and one million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvin20181_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvin20181-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson20183_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson20183-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> The PKI was blamed for the coup and effectively destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003107â109_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003107â109-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991280â283,_284,_287â290_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991280â283,_284,_287â290-63">[61]</a></sup> Suharto capitalised on Sukarno's weakened position, and following a <a href="/wiki/Transition_to_the_New_Order" title="Transition to the New Order">drawn-out power play with Sukarno</a>, Suharto was appointed president in March 1968. His <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(Indonesia)" title="New Order (Indonesia)">"New Order"</a> administration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> supported by the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvin20189â10_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvin20189â10-65">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers2005163_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers2005163-66">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> encouraged <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson2018206_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson2018206-69">[67]</a></sup> which was a crucial factor in the subsequent three decades of substantial economic growth.
</p><p>Indonesia was the country hardest hit by the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> It brought out <a href="/wiki/May_1998_riots_of_Indonesia#Background" title="May 1998 riots of Indonesia">popular discontent</a> with the New Order's corruption and suppression of political opposition and ultimately ended Suharto's presidency.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_45-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-45'>[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_71-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers2005[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-71'>[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchwarz1994[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_72-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchwarz1994[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_October_2020]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(October_2020)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-72'>[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> In 1999, East Timor seceded from Indonesia, following its <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">1975 invasion by Indonesia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">25-year occupation</a> marked by international condemnation of <a href="/wiki/East_Timor_genocide" title="East Timor genocide">human rights abuses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1998, democratic processes have been strengthened by enhancing regional autonomy and instituting the country's <a href="/wiki/2004_Indonesian_presidential_election" title="2004 Indonesian presidential election">first direct presidential election in 2004</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> Political, economic and social instability, corruption, and instances of <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Indonesia" title="Terrorism in Indonesia">terrorism</a> remained problems in the 2000s; however, the economy has performed strongly in the last 15 years. Although relations among the diverse population are mostly harmonious, acute sectarian discontent and violence remain problematic in some areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIP_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIP-77">[75]</a></sup> A political settlement to an armed separatist conflict in <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a> was achieved in 2005 following the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami</a> that killed 130,000 Indonesians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcehPeace_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-AcehPeace-78">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Indonesia" title="Geography of Indonesia">Geography of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Indonesia" title="List of islands of Indonesia">List of islands of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg/220px-Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg/330px-Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg/440px-Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bromo-Semeru-Batok-Widodaren.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Semeru" title="Semeru">Mount Semeru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Bromo" title="Mount Bromo">Mount Bromo</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Java" title="East Java">East Java</a>. Indonesia's seismic and volcanic activity is among the world's highest.</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_parallel_south" title="11th parallel south">11Â°S</a> and <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6Â°N</a> and longitudes <a href="/wiki/95th_meridian_east" title="95th meridian east">95Â°E</a> and <a href="/wiki/141st_meridian_east" title="141st meridian east">141Â°E</a>. It is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Archipelagic_state" title="Archipelagic state">Archipelagic state</a>, extending 5,120 kilometres (3,181Â mi) from east to west and 1,760 kilometres (1,094Â mi) from north to south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuoni199988_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuoni199988-79">[77]</a></sup> The country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coordinating_Ministry_for_Maritime_and_Investments_Affairs_(Indonesia)" title="Coordinating Ministry for Maritime and Investments Affairs (Indonesia)">Coordinating Ministry for Maritime and Investments Affairs</a> says Indonesia has 17,504 islands (with 16,056 registered at the UN)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> scattered over both sides of the equator, around 6,000 of which are inhabited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-81">[79]</a></sup> The largest are <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> (shared with Brunei and Malaysia), <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> (shared with Papua New Guinea).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> Indonesia shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_border" title="IndonesiaâMalaysia border">Malaysia</a> on Borneo and <a href="/wiki/Sebatik_Island" title="Sebatik Island">Sebatik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Papua_New_Guinea_border" title="IndonesiaâPapua New Guinea border">Papua New Guinea</a> on the island of New Guinea, <a href="/wiki/East_Timor%E2%80%93Indonesia_border" title="East TimorâIndonesia border">East Timor</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>, and maritime borders with <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, Malaysia, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.
</p><p>At 4,884 metres (16,024Â ft), <a href="/wiki/Puncak_Jaya" title="Puncak Jaya">Puncak Jaya</a> is Indonesia's highest peak, and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Toba" title="Lake Toba">Lake Toba</a> in Sumatra is the largest lake, with an area of 1,145 km2 (442 sq mi). <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Indonesia" title="List of rivers of Indonesia">Indonesia's largest rivers</a> are in Kalimantan and <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a> and include <a href="/wiki/Kapuas_River" title="Kapuas River">Kapuas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barito_River" title="Barito River">Barito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamberamo_River" title="Mamberamo River">Mamberamo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sepik_River" title="Sepik River">Sepik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahakam_River" title="Mahakam River">Mahakam</a>. They serve as communication and transport links between the island's river settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Indonesia" title="Climate of Indonesia">Climate of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Indonesia" title="Climate change in Indonesia">Climate change in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg/220px-Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg/330px-Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg/440px-Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gunung_Palung_Jungle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rainforest in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Palung_National_Park" title="Mount Palung National Park">Mount Palung National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia lies along the equator, and its climate tends to be relatively even year-round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> Indonesia has two seasonsâa <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>âwith no extremes of summer or winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldbank1_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-85">[83]</a></sup> For most of Indonesia, the dry season falls between May and October, with the wet season between November and April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldbank1_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank1-85">[83]</a></sup> Indonesia's climate is almost entirely <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a>, dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> found on every large island of Indonesia. More cooling climate types do exist in mountainous regions that are 1,300 to 1,500 metres (4,300 to 4,900 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">feet</a>) above sea level. The oceanic climate (KÃ¶ppen <i>Cfb</i>) prevails in highland areas adjacent to rainforest climates, with reasonably uniform precipitation year-round. In highland areas near the tropical monsoon and tropical savanna climates, the subtropical highland climate (KÃ¶ppen <i>Cwb</i>) is prevalent with a more pronounced dry season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1816" decoding="async" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_IDN_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen-Geiger climate classification</a> map for Indonesia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Some regions, such as <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, experience only slight differences in rainfall and temperature between the seasons, whereas others, such as Nusa Tenggara, experience far more pronounced differences with droughts in the dry season and floods in the wet. Rainfall varies across regions, with more in western Sumatra, Java, and the interiors of Kalimantan and Papua, and less in areas closer to Australia, such as Nusa Tenggara, which tends to be dry. The almost uniformly warm waters that constitute 81% of Indonesia's area ensure that land temperatures remain relatively constant. <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">Humidity</a> is quite high, at between 70 and 90%. Winds are moderate and generally predictable, with <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoons</a> usually blowing in from the south and east in June through October and from the northwest in November through March. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">Typhoons</a> and large-scale storms pose little hazard to mariners; significant dangers come from swift currents in channels, such as the <a href="/wiki/Lombok_Strait" title="Lombok Strait">Lombok</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sape_Strait" title="Sape Strait">Sape</a> straits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several studies consider Indonesia to be at severe risk from the <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Indonesia" title="Climate change in Indonesia">projected effects of climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> These include unreduced emissions resulting in an average temperature rise of around 1Â Â°C (2Â Â°F) by mid-century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ImpLab_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-ImpLab-89">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimChng_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClimChng-90">[88]</a></sup> raising the frequency of drought and food shortages (with an impact on precipitation and the patterns of wet and dry seasons, and thus Indonesia's agriculture system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimChng_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-ClimChng-90">[88]</a></sup>) as well as numerous diseases and wildfires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimChng_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-ClimChng-90">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">Rising sea levels</a> would also threaten most of Indonesia's population, who live in low-lying coastal areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClimChng_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-ClimChng-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> Impoverished communities would likely be affected the most by climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Indonesia" title="Geology of Indonesia">Geology of Indonesia</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanoes_of_Indonesia" title="Volcanoes of Indonesia">Volcanoes of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geology_indonesia_map.jpg"><img alt="Geology indonesia map.jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1273" data-file-width="2051" decoding="async" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geology_indonesia_map.jpg/310px-Geology_indonesia_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geology_indonesia_map.jpg/465px-Geology_indonesia_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Geology_indonesia_map.jpg/620px-Geology_indonesia_map.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geology_indonesia_map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">Tectonically</a>, most of Indonesia's area is highly unstable, making it a site of numerous volcanoes and frequent earthquakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VolEthQ_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-VolEthQ-94">[92]</a></sup> It lies on the Pacific <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Australian_Plate" title="Indo-Australian Plate">Indo-Australian Plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">Pacific Plate</a> are pushed under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_plate" title="Eurasian plate">Eurasian plate</a>, where they melt at about 100 kilometres (62 miles) deep. A string of volcanoes runs through Sumatra, <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nusa_Tenggara" title="Nusa Tenggara">Nusa Tenggara</a>, and then to the <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">Banda Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku</a> to northeastern <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton200338_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton200338-95">[93]</a></sup> Of the 400 volcanoes, around 130 are active.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VolEthQ_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-VolEthQ-94">[92]</a></sup> Between 1972 and 1991, there were 29 volcanic eruptions, mostly on Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">Volcanic ash</a> has made agricultural conditions unpredictable in some areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> However, it has also resulted in fertile soils, a factor in historically sustaining the high population densities of Java and Bali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Toba_catastrophe_theory" title="Toba catastrophe theory">massive supervolcano erupted</a> at present-day <a href="/wiki/Lake_Toba" title="Lake Toba">Lake Toba</a> around 70,000 BCE. It is believed to have caused a global <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_winter" title="Volcanic winter">volcanic winter</a> and cooling of the climate and subsequently led to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_bottleneck" title="Genetic bottleneck">genetic bottleneck</a> in human evolution, though this is still in debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1815_eruption_of_Mount_Tambora" title="1815 eruption of Mount Tambora">1815 eruption of Mount Tambora</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1883_eruption_of_Krakatoa" title="1883 eruption of Krakatoa">1883 eruption of Krakatoa</a> were among the largest in recorded history. The former caused 92,000 deaths and created an umbrella of volcanic ash that spread and blanketed parts of the archipelago and made much of the Northern Hemisphere <a href="/wiki/Year_Without_a_Summer" title="Year Without a Summer">without summer in 1816</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> The latter produced the loudest sound in recorded history and caused 36,000 deaths due to the eruption itself and the resulting tsunamis, with significant additional effects around the world years after the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> Recent catastrophic disasters due to seismic activity include the 2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and the <a href="/wiki/2006_Yogyakarta_earthquake" title="2006 Yogyakarta earthquake">2006 Yogyakarta earthquake</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_conservation">Biodiversity and conservation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Indonesia" title="Fauna of Indonesia">Fauna of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Indonesia" title="Flora of Indonesia">Flora of Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Indonesia" title="Protected areas of Indonesia">Protected areas of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:164px;max-width:164px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1794" data-file-width="2394" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG/162px-Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG/243px-Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG/324px-Rafflesia_arnoldi_2013-12-31_21-48.JPG 2x" width="162"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:124px;max-width:124px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:121px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Man_of_the_woods.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1284" data-file-width="1296" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Man_of_the_woods.JPG/122px-Man_of_the_woods.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Man_of_the_woods.JPG/183px-Man_of_the_woods.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Man_of_the_woods.JPG/244px-Man_of_the_woods.JPG 2x" width="122"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:102px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Komodo_dragon_(Varanus_komodoensis).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2895" data-file-width="3670" decoding="async" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg/130px-Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg/195px-Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg/260px-Komodo_dragon_%28Varanus_komodoensis%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:156px;max-width:156px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:102px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg/154px-Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg/231px-Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg/308px-Paradisaea_apoda_-Bali_Bird_Park-6.jpg 2x" width="154"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Species endemic to Indonesia. Clockwise from top: <i><a href="/wiki/Rafflesia_arnoldii" title="Rafflesia arnoldii">Rafflesia arnoldii</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">orangutan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_bird-of-paradise" title="Greater bird-of-paradise">greater bird-of-paradise</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Komodo_dragon" title="Komodo dragon">Komodo dragon</a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia's size, tropical climate, and archipelagic geography support one of the world's highest levels of biodiversity, and it is among the 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> identified by <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>. Its flora and fauna are a mixture of Asian and <a href="/wiki/Australasian_realm" title="Australasian realm">Australasian</a> species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Shelf" title="Sunda Shelf">Sunda Shelf</a> islands (Sumatra, Java, Borneo, and Bali) were once linked to mainland Asia and have a wealth of Asian fauna. Large species such as the <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_tiger" title="Sumatran tiger">Sumatran tiger</a>, rhinoceros, orangutan, <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a>, and leopard were once abundant as far east as Bali, but numbers and distribution have dwindled drastically. Having been long separated from the continental landmasses, Sulawesi, Nusa Tenggara, and Maluku have developed their unique flora and fauna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> Papua was part of the Australian landmass and is home to a <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_New_Guinea" title="Fauna of New Guinea">unique fauna and flora</a> closely related to that of Australia, including over 600 bird species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia is second only to Australia in terms of total endemic species, with 36% of its 1,531 species of bird and 39% of its 515 species of mammal being endemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> Tropical seas surround Indonesia's 80,000 kilometres (50,000 miles) of coastline. The country has a range of sea and coastal ecosystems, including <a href="/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_Indonesia" title="List of beaches in Indonesia">beaches</a>, dunes, estuaries, mangroves, coral reefs, seagrass beds, coastal mudflats, tidal flats, algal beds, and small island ecosystems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EcoSeas1_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-EcoSeas1-16">[14]</a></sup> Indonesia is one of the <a href="/wiki/Coral_Triangle" title="Coral Triangle">Coral Triangle</a> countries with the world's most enormous diversity of <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef_fish" title="Coral reef fish">coral reef fish</a>, with more than 1,650 species in eastern Indonesia only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>British naturalist <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Russel_Wallace" title="Alfred Russel Wallace">Alfred Russel Wallace</a> described a dividing line (<a href="/wiki/Wallace_Line" title="Wallace Line">Wallace Line</a>) between the distribution of Indonesia's Asian and Australasian species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Severin_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Severin-108">[106]</a></sup> It runs roughly northâsouth along the edge of the Sunda Shelf, between Kalimantan and Sulawesi, and along the deep <a href="/wiki/Lombok_Strait" title="Lombok Strait">Lombok Strait</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a> and Bali. Flora and fauna on the west of the line are generally Asian, while east from Lombok is increasingly Australian until the tipping point at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weber_Line" title="Weber Line">Weber Line</a>. In his 1869 book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Malay_Archipelago" title="The Malay Archipelago">The Malay Archipelago</a></i>, Wallace described numerous species unique to the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> The region of islands between his line and New Guinea is now termed <a href="/wiki/Wallacea" title="Wallacea">Wallacea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Severin_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Severin-108">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg/220px-Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg/330px-Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg/440px-Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riau_palm_oil_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Deforestation in Riau province, <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, to make way for an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_palm" title="Oil palm">oil palm</a> plantation (2007).</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia's large and growing population and rapid industrialisation present serious <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Indonesia" title="Environmental issues in Indonesia">environmental issues</a>. They are often given a lower priority due to high poverty levels and weak, under-resourced governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forestprob_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-forestprob-110">[108]</a></sup> Problems include the destruction of peatlands, large-scale illegal <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> (causing <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_haze" title="Southeast Asian haze">extensive haze across parts of Southeast Asia</a>), over-exploitation of marine resources, air pollution, garbage management, and reliable <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Indonesia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Indonesia">water and wastewater services</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forestprob_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-forestprob-110">[108]</a></sup> These issues contribute to Indonesia's low ranking (number 116 out of 180 countries) in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a>. The report also indicates that Indonesia's performance is generally below average in both regional and global context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has one of the world's fastest deforestation rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sust_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-sust-112">[110]</a></sup> In 2020, forests covered approximately 49.1% of the country's land area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> down from 87% in 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landuse_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-landuse-114">[112]</a></sup> Since the 1970s, log production, various plantations and agriculture have been responsible for much of the <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Indonesia" title="Deforestation in Indonesia">deforestation in Indonesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-landuse_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-landuse-114">[112]</a></sup> Most recently, it has been driven by the <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> industry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> which has been criticised for its environmental impact and displacement of local communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sust_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-sust-112">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The situation has made Indonesia the world's largest forest-based emitter of greenhouse gases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> It also threatens the survival of indigenous and endemic species. The <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> (IUCN) identified 140 species of mammals as <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened</a> and 15 as critically endangered, including the <a href="/wiki/Bali_myna" title="Bali myna">Bali myna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sumatran_orangutan" title="Sumatran orangutan">Sumatran orangutan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Javan_rhinoceros" title="Javan rhinoceros">Javan rhinoceros</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Indonesia" title="Politics of Indonesia">Politics of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ruang_MPR.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2082" data-file-width="3131" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruang_MPR.jpg/220px-Ruang_MPR.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruang_MPR.jpg/330px-Ruang_MPR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruang_MPR.jpg/440px-Ruang_MPR.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ruang_MPR.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A presidential inauguration by the MPR in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DPR/MPR_Building" title="DPR/MPR Building">Parliament Complex</a> Jakarta, <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Joko_Widodo" title="First inauguration of Joko Widodo">2014</a></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia is a republic with a presidential system. Following the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Suharto" title="Fall of Suharto">fall of the New Order</a> in 1998, political and governmental structures have undergone sweeping reforms, with <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Indonesia#Constitutional_amendments" title="Constitution of Indonesia">four constitutional amendments</a> revamping the executive, legislative and judicial branches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harijanti2006_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harijanti2006-121">[119]</a></sup> Chief among them is the delegation of power and authority to various regional entities while remaining a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">President of Indonesia</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian National Armed Forces</a> (<i>Tentara Nasional Indonesia</i>, TNI), and the director of domestic governance, policy-making, and foreign affairs. The president may serve a maximum of two consecutive five-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>The highest representative body at the national level is the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Consultative_Assembly" title="People's Consultative Assembly">People's Consultative Assembly</a> (<i>Majelis Permusyawaratan Rakyat</i>, MPR). Its main functions are supporting and amending the constitution, inaugurating and impeaching the president,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UUD45_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-UUD45-125">[123]</a></sup> and formalising broad outlines of state policy. The MPR comprises two houses; the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Representative_Council" title="People's Representative Council">People's Representative Council</a> (<i>Dewan Perwakilan Rakyat</i>, DPR), with 575 members, and the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Representative_Council" title="Regional Representative Council">Regional Representative Council</a> (<i>Dewan Perwakilan Daerah</i>, DPD), with 136.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INAlegis_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-INAlegis-126">[124]</a></sup> The DPR passes legislation and monitors the executive branch. Reforms since 1998 have markedly increased its role in national governance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harijanti2006_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Harijanti2006-121">[119]</a></sup> while the DPD is a new chamber for matters of regional management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UUD45_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-UUD45-125">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most civil disputes appear before the State Court (<i>Pengadilan Negeri</i>); appeals are heard before the High Court (<i>Pengadilan Tinggi</i>). The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Indonesia" title="Supreme Court of Indonesia">Supreme Court of Indonesia</a> (<i>Mahkamah Agung</i>) is the highest level of the judicial branch and hears final cessation appeals and conducts case reviews. Other courts include the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Indonesia" title="Constitutional Court of Indonesia">Constitutional Court</a> (<i>Mahkamah Konstitusi</i>) which listens to constitutional and political matters, and the Religious Court (<i>Pengadilan Agama</i>), which deals with codified Islamic Personal Law (<i>sharia</i>) cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Commission_of_Indonesia" title="Judicial Commission of Indonesia">Judicial Commission</a> (<i>Komisi Yudisial</i>) monitors the performance of judges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parties_and_elections">Parties and elections</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Indonesia" title="List of political parties in Indonesia">List of political parties in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Indonesia" title="Elections in Indonesia">Elections in Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:124px;max-width:124px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:146px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5246" data-file-width="4364" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg/122px-Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg/183px-Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg/244px-Joko_Widodo_2019_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="122"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a><br/><small>7th <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">President of Indonesia</a><br/></small></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:124px;max-width:124px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:146px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5237" data-file-width="4359" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg/122px-Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg/183px-Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg/244px-Ma%27ruf_Amin_2019_official_portrait.jpg 2x" width="122"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center"><a href="/wiki/Ma%27ruf_Amin" title="Ma'ruf Amin">Ma'ruf Amin</a><br/><small>13th <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Indonesia" title="Vice President of Indonesia">Vice President of Indonesia</a><br/></small></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Since 1999, Indonesia has had a multi-party system. In all <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Indonesia" title="Elections in Indonesia">legislative elections</a> since the fall of the <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(Indonesia)" title="New Order (Indonesia)">New Order</a>, no political party has won an overall majority of seats. The <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Democratic_Party_of_Struggle" title="Indonesian Democratic Party of Struggle">Indonesian Democratic Party of Struggle</a> (PDI-P), which secured the most votes in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Indonesian_general_election" title="2019 Indonesian general election">2019 elections</a>, is the party of the incumbent president, <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> Other notable parties include the <a href="/wiki/Golkar" title="Golkar">Party of the Functional Groups</a> (<i>Golkar</i>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Indonesia_Movement_Party" title="Great Indonesia Movement Party">Great Indonesia Movement Party</a> (<i>Gerindra</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Indonesia)" title="Democratic Party (Indonesia)">Democratic Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Prosperous_Justice_Party" title="Prosperous Justice Party">Prosperous Justice Party</a> (PKS).
</p><p>The first general election was held in 1955 to elect members of the DPR and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Assembly_of_Indonesia" title="Constitutional Assembly of Indonesia">Constitutional Assembly</a> (<i>Konstituante</i>). The most recent elections in 2019 resulted in nine political parties in the DPR, with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Election_threshold" title="Election threshold">parliamentary threshold</a> of 4% of the national vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> At the national level, Indonesians did not elect a president until 2004. Since then, the president is elected for a five-year term, as are the party-aligned members of the DPR and the non-partisan DPD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INAlegis_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-INAlegis-126">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harijanti2006_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-Harijanti2006-121">[119]</a></sup> Beginning with the <a href="/wiki/2015_Indonesian_local_elections" title="2015 Indonesian local elections">2015 local elections</a>, elections for governors and mayors have occurred on the same date. In 2014, the Constitutional Court ruled that legislative and presidential elections would be held simultaneously, starting in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Indonesia" title="Subdivisions of Indonesia">Subdivisions of Indonesia</a></div>
<p>Indonesia has several levels of subdivisions. The first level are the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">provinces</a>, which have a legislature (<i>Dewan Perwakilan Rakyat Daerah</i>, DPRD) and an elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_governors_in_Indonesia" title="List of current governors in Indonesia">governor</a>. A total of 37 provinces have been established from the original eight in 1945,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> with the most recent change being the split of <a href="/wiki/Central_Papua" title="Central Papua">Central Papua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highland_Papua" title="Highland Papua">Highland Papua</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Papua" title="South Papua">South Papua</a> from <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">Papua</a> in 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The second level are the <a href="/wiki/Regency_(Indonesia)" title="Regency (Indonesia)">regencies</a> (<i>kabupaten</i>) and <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_Indonesia" title="City status in Indonesia">cities</a> (<i>kota</i>), led by regents (<i>bupati</i>) and mayors (<i>walikota</i>) respectively and a legislature (<i>DPRD Kabupaten/Kota</i>). The third level are the <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Indonesia" title="Districts of Indonesia">districts</a> (<i>kecamatan</i>, <i>distrik</i> in <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Papua</a>, or <i>kapanewon</i> and <i>kemantren</i> in <a href="/wiki/Special_Region_of_Yogyakarta" title="Special Region of Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a>), and the fourth are the <a href="/wiki/Villages_of_Indonesia" title="Villages of Indonesia">villages</a> (either <i>desa</i>, <i>kelurahan</i>, <i>kampung</i>, <i>nagari</i> in <a href="/wiki/West_Sumatra" title="West Sumatra">West Sumatra</a>, or <i>gampong</i> in <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup>
</p><p>The village is the lowest level of government administration. It is divided into several community groups (<i>rukun warga</i>, RW), which are further divided into neighbourhood groups (<i>rukun tetangga</i>, RT). In Java, the village (<i>desa</i>) is divided into smaller units called <i>dusun</i> or <i>dukuh</i> (hamlets), which are the same as RW. Following the implementation of regional autonomy measures in 2001, regencies and cities have become chief administrative units responsible for providing most government services. The village administration level is the most influential on a citizen's daily life and handles village or neighbourhood matters through an elected village head (<i>lurah</i> or <i>kepala desa</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>Eight provincesâAceh, Jakarta, Yogyakarta, <a href="/wiki/Papua_(province)" title="Papua (province)">Papua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Papua" title="Central Papua">Central Papua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highland_Papua" title="Highland Papua">Highland Papua</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Papua" title="South Papua">South Papua</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West Papua</a>âare granted a <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">special autonomous status</a> (<i>otonomi khusus</i>) from the central government. A conservative <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamic territory</a>, Aceh has the right to create some aspects of an independent legal system implementing <i><a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> Jakarta is the only <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">city with a provincial government</a> due to its position as the <a href="/wiki/Capital_of_Indonesia" title="Capital of Indonesia">capital of Indonesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> Yogyakarta is the only <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_monarchies" title="List of Indonesian monarchies">pre-colonial monarchy</a> legally recognised within Indonesia, with the positions of governor and vice governor being prioritised for the reigning <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta_Sultanate" title="Yogyakarta Sultanate">Sultan of Yogyakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakualaman" title="Pakualaman">Duke of Pakualaman</a>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> The five Papuan provinces are the only ones where the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people_of_New_Guinea" title="Indigenous people of New Guinea">indigenous people</a> have privileges in their local government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable relarticle mainarticle selfreference noprint" role="note">This section is <a href="/wiki/Help:Transclusion" title="Help:Transclusion">transcluded</a> from <a href="/wiki/Template:Indonesia_provinces_labelled_map" title="Template:Indonesia provinces labelled map">Template:Indonesia provinces labelled map</a>. <span class="plainlinks" style="font-style: normal; font-size:85%;">(<a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Indonesia_provinces_labelled_map&amp;action=edit">edit</a> | <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Indonesia_provinces_labelled_map&amp;action=history">history</a>)</span></div>
