<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Indonesia" title="Foreign relations of Indonesia">Foreign relations of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/220px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/330px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg/440px-Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Australias_indonesian_embassy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Indonesia,_Canberra" title="Embassy of Indonesia, Canberra">Embassy of Indonesia, Canberra</a>, Australia</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia maintains 132 diplomatic missions abroad, including 95 embassies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> The country adheres to what it calls a "free and active" foreign policy, seeking a role in regional affairs in proportion to its size and location but avoiding involvement in conflicts among other countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia was a significant battleground during the Cold War. Numerous attempts by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> to some degree,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> culminated in the 1965 coup attempt and subsequent upheaval that led to a reorientation of foreign policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson2018_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson2018-147">[145]</a></sup> Quiet alignment with the Western world while maintaining a non-aligned stance has characterised Indonesia's foreign policy since then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> Today, it maintains close relations with its neighbours and is a founding member of the Association of Southeast Asian Nations (<a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>. In common with most of the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>, Indonesia does not have diplomatic relations with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and has actively supported <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>. However, observers have pointed out that Indonesia has ties with Israel, albeit discreetly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has been <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_and_the_United_Nations" title="Indonesia and the United Nations">a member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1950<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn2_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-fn2-151">[c]</a></sup> and was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (NAM) and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup> Indonesia is a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Free_Trade_Area" title="ASEAN Free Trade Area">ASEAN Free Trade Area</a> agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Cairns_Group" title="Cairns Group">Cairns Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), and an occasional <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> Indonesia has been a humanitarian and development aid recipient since 1967,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[152]</a></sup> and recently, the country established its first overseas aid program in late 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian National Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Indonesia" title="Military history of Indonesia">Military history of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:139px;max-width:139px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tniadkostrad.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="91" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Tniadkostrad.jpg/274px-Tniadkostrad.jpg 2x" width="137"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:149px;max-width:149px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="359" data-file-width="581" decoding="async" height="91" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg/294px-Tni-au_su-30_1.jpg 2x" width="147"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:140px;max-width:140px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG/138px-RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG/276px-RAN-IFR_2013_D3_83.JPG 2x" width="138"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:148px;max-width:148px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:91px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/146px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/219px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg/292px-Pindad_Anoa_APS-3_RLG.jpg 2x" width="146"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Indonesian Armed Forces. Clockwise from top: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Army" title="Indonesian Army">Indonesian Army</a> during training session, <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-30" title="Sukhoi Su-30">Sukhoi Su-30</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anoa_(armoured_personnel_carrier)" title="Anoa (armoured personnel carrier)">Pindad Anoa</a>, and Indonesian naval vessel <a href="/wiki/KRI_Sultan_Iskandar_Muda_(367)" title="KRI Sultan Iskandar Muda (367)">KRIÂ <i>Sultan Iskandar Muda</i>Â <span class="nowrap">(367)</span></a>.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia's Armed Forces (TNI) include the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Army" title="Indonesian Army">Army</a> (TNIâAD), <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Navy" title="Indonesian Navy">Navy</a> (TNIâAL, which includes <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Marine_Corps" title="Indonesian Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Air_Force" title="Indonesian Air Force">Air Force</a> (TNIâAU). The army has about 400,000 active-duty personnel. Defence spending in the national budget was 0.7% of GDP in 2018,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> with controversial involvement of military-owned commercial interests and foundations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup> The Armed Forces were formed during the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">Indonesian National Revolution</a> when it undertook guerrilla warfare along with informal militia. Since then, territorial lines have formed the basis of all TNI branches' structure, aimed at maintaining domestic stability and deterring foreign threats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup> The military has possessed a strong political influence since its founding, which <a href="/wiki/Dwifungsi" title="Dwifungsi">peaked during the New Order</a>. Political reforms in 1998 included the removal of the TNI's formal representation from the legislature. Nevertheless, its political influence remains, albeit at a reduced level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since independence, the country has struggled to maintain unity against local insurgencies and separatist movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> Some, notably in <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_Aceh" title="Insurgency in Aceh">Aceh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua</a>, have led to an armed conflict and subsequent allegations of human rights abuses and brutality from all sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriend2003270â273,_477â480_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriend2003270â273,_477â480-163">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup> The former was resolved peacefully in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AcehPeace_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-AcehPeace-78">[76]</a></sup> while the latter has continued amid a significant, albeit imperfect, implementation of regional autonomy laws and a reported decline in the levels of violence and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Indonesia#West_Papua_issues" title="Human rights in Indonesia">human rights abuses</a> as of 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup> Other engagements of the army include the <a href="/wiki/West_New_Guinea_dispute" title="West New Guinea dispute">conflict</a> against the Netherlands over the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_New_Guinea" title="Dutch New Guinea">Dutch New Guinea</a>, the opposition to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a>-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Agreement" title="Malaysia Agreement">creation of Malaysia</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="IndonesiaâMalaysia confrontation">Konfrontasi</a>"), the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965â66">mass killings</a> of the Indonesian Communist Party (PKI), and the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">invasion of East Timor</a>, which remains Indonesia's most massive military operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[164]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Indonesia" title="Economy of Indonesia">Economy of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Indonesia" title="Economic history of Indonesia">Economic history of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Indonesia" title="Agriculture in Indonesia">Agriculture in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/220px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/330px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg/440px-Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oil_palm_plantation_in_Cigudeg-03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vast <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> plantation in <a href="/wiki/Bogor_Regency" title="Bogor Regency">Bogor Regency</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>. Indonesia is the world's largest producer of palm oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/290px-Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/435px-Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/580px-Indonesia_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Indonesia exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> in which the private sector and government play vital roles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup> As the only <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a> member state in Southeast Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[167]</a></sup> the country has the largest economy in the region and is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newly_industrialised_country" title="Newly industrialised country">newly industrialised country</a>. Per a 2022 estimate, it is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">17th largest economy by nominal GDP</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">7th in terms of GDP at PPP</a>, estimated to be <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1.289 trillion and <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>3.995 trillion, respectively. Per capita GDP in PPP is <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>14,535, while nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">per capita GDP</a> is <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>4,691.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMF_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-IMF-9">[9]</a></sup> Services are the economy's largest sector and account for 43.4% of GDP (2018), followed by industry (39.7%) and agriculture (12.8%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup> Since 2009, it has employed more people than other sectors, accounting for 47.7% of the total labour force, followed by agriculture (30.2%) and industry (21.9%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over time, the structure of the economy has changed considerably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBA_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-173">[170]</a></sup> Historically, it has been weighted heavily towards agriculture, reflecting both its stage of economic development and government policies in the 1950s and 1960s to promote agricultural self-sufficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBA_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-173">[170]</a></sup> A gradual process of industrialisation and urbanisation began in the late 1960s and accelerated in the 1980s as falling oil prices saw the government focus on diversifying away from oil exports and towards manufactured exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBA_173-2"><a href="#cite_note-RBA-173">[170]</a></sup> This development continued throughout the 1980s and into the next decade despite the <a href="/wiki/1990_oil_price_shock" title="1990 oil price shock">1990 oil price shock</a>, during which the GDP rose at an average rate of 7.1%. As a result, the official poverty rate fell from 60% to 15%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> Trade barriers reduction from the mid-1980s made the economy more globally integrated. The growth ended with the <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis" title="1997 Asian financial crisis">1997 Asian financial crisis</a> that severely impacted the economy, including a 13.1% real GDP contraction in 1998 and a 78% inflation. The economy reached its low point in mid-1999 with only 0.8% real GDP growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>Relatively steady inflation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup> and an increase in GDP deflator and the Consumer Price Index<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> have contributed to strong economic growth in recent years. From 2007 to 2019, annual growth accelerated to between 4% and 6% due to improvements in the banking sector and domestic consumption,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> helping Indonesia weather the 2008â2009 <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> and regain in 2011 the investment grade rating it had lost in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 9.41% of the population lived below the poverty line, and the official open unemployment rate was 5.28%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> During the first year of the global <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, the economy suffered its first recession since the 1997 crisis but recovered in the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has abundant natural resources. Its primary industries are fishing, petroleum, timber, paper products, cotton cloth, tourism, petroleum mining, natural gas, bauxite, coal and tin. Its main agricultural products are rice, coconuts, soybeans, bananas, coffee, tea, palm, rubber, and sugar cane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup> These commodities make up a large portion of the country's exports, with palm oil and coal briquettes as the leading export commodities. In addition to refined and crude petroleum as the primary imports, telephones, vehicle parts and wheat cover the majority of additional imports. China, the United States, Japan, Singapore, India, Malaysia, South Korea and Thailand are Indonesia's principal export markets and import partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Indonesia" title="Transport in Indonesia">Transport in Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:138px;max-width:138px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:98px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1592" data-file-width="2196" decoding="async" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/136px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/204px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg/272px-TransJakarta_Bundaran_HI_1.jpg 2x" width="136"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:150px;max-width:150px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:98px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1624" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/148px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/222px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG/296px-KRL_Jabotabek_6115_Gambir_20111126.JPG 2x" width="148"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:106px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/142px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/213px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg/284px-Pelni_Einschiffung.jpg 2x" width="142"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:144px;max-width:144px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:106px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3(ER)_cn29147,_Take_off_from_Schiphol_(AMS_-_EHAM),_The_Netherlands.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2086" data-file-width="2778" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG/142px-PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG/213px-PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG/284px-PK-GIE_Garuda_Indonesia_Boeing_777-3U3%28ER%29_cn29147%2C_Take_off_from_Schiphol_%28AMS_-_EHAM%29%2C_The_Netherlands.JPG 2x" width="142"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Major transport modes in Indonesia. Clockwise from top: <a href="/wiki/TransJakarta" title="TransJakarta">TransJakarta</a> bus, <a href="/wiki/KRL_Commuterline" title="KRL Commuterline">KRL Commuterline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a> Boeing 777â300 ER, <a href="/wiki/Pelni" title="Pelni">Pelni</a> ship.</div></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia's transport system has been shaped over time by the economic resource base of an archipelago and the distribution of its 275Â million people highly concentrated on <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup> All transport modes play a role in the country's transport system and are generally complementary rather than competitive. In 2016, the transport sector generated about 5.2% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>The road transport system is predominant, with a total length of 542,310 kilometres (336,980 miles) as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup> Jakarta has the <a href="/wiki/TransJakarta" title="TransJakarta">most extended bus rapid transit system globally</a>, boasting 251.2 kilometres (156.1 miles) in 13 corridors and ten cross-corridor routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rickshaw" title="Rickshaw">Rickshaws</a> such as <i>bajaj</i> and <i>becak</i> and <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">share taxis</a> such as <i>Angkot</i> and <i>Metromini</i> are a regular sight in the country.
</p><p>Most <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Indonesia" title="Rail transport in Indonesia">railways</a> are in Java, used for freight and passenger transport, such as local commuter rail services (mainly in <a href="/wiki/KRL_Commuterline" title="KRL Commuterline">Jakarta</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KRL_Commuterline_Yogyakarta%E2%80%93Solo" title="KRL Commuterline YogyakartaâSolo">YogyakartaâSolo</a>) complementing the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Indonesia" title="Rail transport in Indonesia">inter-city rail network</a> in several cities. In the late 2010s, Jakarta and Palembang were the first cities in Indonesia to have <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> systems, with more planned for other cities in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup> In 2015, the government announced a plan to build a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_Indonesia" title="High-speed rail in Indonesia">high-speed rail</a>, which would be the first in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[187]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia's largest airport, <a href="/wiki/Soekarno%E2%80%93Hatta_International_Airport" title="SoekarnoâHatta International Airport">SoekarnoâHatta International Airport</a>, is among the busiest in the Southern Hemisphere, <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">serving 54Â million passengers in 2019</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ngurah_Rai_International_Airport" title="Ngurah Rai International Airport">Ngurah Rai International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juanda_International_Airport" title="Juanda International Airport">Juanda International Airport</a> are the country's second-and third-busiest airport, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a>, the country's flag carrier since 1949, is one of the world's leading airlines and a member of the global airline alliance <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Tanjung_Priok" title="Port of Tanjung Priok">Port of Tanjung Priok</a> is the busiest and most advanced Indonesian port,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[188]</a></sup> handling more than 50% of Indonesia's trans-shipment cargo traffic.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Indonesia" title="Energy in Indonesia">Energy in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pltb-sidrap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="862" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Pltb-sidrap.jpg/220px-Pltb-sidrap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Pltb-sidrap.jpg/330px-Pltb-sidrap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Pltb-sidrap.jpg/440px-Pltb-sidrap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pltb-sidrap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sidrap wind farm, Indonesia's first wind power plant, in Sidrap Regency, <a href="/wiki/South_Sulawesi" title="South Sulawesi">South Sulawesi</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2017, Indonesia was the world's 9th largest energy producer with 4,200 <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt-hour" title="Kilowatt-hour">terawatt-hours</a> (14.2Â <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000000000000000_(number)" title="1000000000000000 (number)">quadrillion</a> <a href="/wiki/British_thermal_unit" title="British thermal unit">British thermal units</a>) and the 15th largest energy consumer, with 2,100 terawatt-hours (7.1Â quadrillion British thermal units).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[189]</a></sup> The country has substantial energy resources, including 22Â billion barrels (3.5Â billion cubic metres) of conventional oil and gas reserves (of which about 4Â billion barrels are recoverable), 8Â billion barrels of oil-equivalent of coal-based methane (CBM) resources, and 28Â billion tonnes of recoverable coal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[190]</a></sup> While reliance on domestic coal and imported oil has increased,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[191]</a></sup> Indonesia has seen progress in renewable energy, with hydropower being the most abundant source. Furthermore, the country has the potential for geothermal, solar, wind, biomass and ocean energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[192]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Indonesia's total national installed power generation capacity stands at 69,678.85 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg/220px-Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg/330px-Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg/440px-Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Another_View_of_Jati_Luhur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jatiluhur_Dam" title="Jatiluhur Dam">Jatiluhur Dam</a>, Indonesia's first and largest dam, in <a href="/wiki/Purwakarta_Regency" title="Purwakarta Regency">Purwakarta Regency</a>, West Java.</div></div></div>
<p>The country's largest dam, <a href="/wiki/Jatiluhur_Dam" title="Jatiluhur Dam">Jatiluhur</a>, has several purposes, including hydroelectric power generation, water supply, flood control, irrigation and <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a>. The earth-fill dam is 105Â m (344Â ft) high and withholds a reservoir of 3.0Â billionÂ m<sup>3</sup> (2.4Â millionÂ acreâft). It helps to supply water to Jakarta and to irrigate 240,000Â ha (590,000 acres) of rice fields<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> and has an installed capacity of 186.5 MW which feeds into the Java grid managed by the State Electricity Company (<i><a href="/wiki/Perusahaan_Listrik_Negara" title="Perusahaan Listrik Negara">Perusahaan Listrik Negara</a></i>, PLN).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Indonesia" title="Science and technology in Indonesia">Science and technology in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2020" data-file-width="2020" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/220px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/330px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg/440px-STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-41-B_Palapa_B-2_deployment.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Palapa" title="Palapa">Palapa</a> satellite launch in 1984</div></div></div>
<p>Government expenditure on research and development is relatively low (0.3% of GDP in 2019),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[195]</a></sup> and Indonesia only ranked 87th (out of 132 economies) on the 2021 <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[196]</a></sup> Historical examples of scientific and technological developments include the paddy cultivation technique <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrace_(agriculture)" title="Terrace (agriculture)"><i>terasering</i></a>, which is common in Southeast Asia, and the <a href="/wiki/Pinisi" title="Pinisi">pinisi</a> boats by the <a href="/wiki/Bugis" title="Bugis">Bugis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Makassar_people" title="Makassar people">Makassar people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup> In the 1980s, Indonesian engineer <a href="/wiki/Tjokorda_Raka_Sukawati" title="Tjokorda Raka Sukawati">Tjokorda Raka Sukawati</a> invented a road construction technique named <a href="/wiki/Sosrobahu" title="Sosrobahu">Sosrobahu</a> that later became widely used in several countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup> The country is also an active producer of passenger trains and freight wagons with its state-owned company, the <a href="/wiki/Industri_Kereta_Api" title="Industri Kereta Api">Indonesian Railway Industry</a> (INKA), and has exported trains abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has a long history of developing military and small commuter aircraft. It is the only country in Southeast Asia to build and produce aircraft. The state-owned <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Aerospace" title="Indonesian Aerospace">Indonesian Aerospace company</a> (<i>PT. Dirgantara Indonesia</i>) has provided components for <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> The company also collaborated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EADS_CASA" title="EADS CASA">EADS CASA</a> of Spain to develop the <a href="/wiki/CASA/IPTN_CN-235" title="CASA/IPTN CN-235">CN-235</a>, which has been used by several countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup> Former President <a href="/wiki/B._J._Habibie" title="B. J. Habibie">B. J. Habibie</a> played a vital role in this achievement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[202]</a></sup> Indonesia has also joined the <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> programme to manufacture the 4.5-generation fighter jet <a href="/wiki/KAI_KF-21_Boramae" title="KAI KF-21 Boramae">KAI KF-21 Boramae</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has a space programme and space agency, the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Aeronautics_and_Space" title="National Institute of Aeronautics and Space">National Institute of Aeronautics and Space</a> (<i>Lembaga Penerbangan dan Antariksa Nasional</i>, LAPAN). In the 1970s, Indonesia became the first developing country to operate a satellite system called <a href="/wiki/Palapa" title="Palapa">Palapa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[204]</a></sup> a series of communication satellites owned by <a href="/wiki/Indosat" title="Indosat">Indosat</a>. The first satellite, PALAPA A1, was launched on 8 July 1976 from the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a> in Florida, United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[205]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Indonesia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Indonesia has launched 18 satellites for various purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Indonesia" title="Tourism in Indonesia">Tourism in Indonesia</a></div><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1108" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/250px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/375px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg/500px-Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Borobudur-Nothwest-view.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a>, the world's largest Buddhist temple, is the single most visited tourist attraction in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Indonesia" title="Tourism in Indonesia">Tourism</a> contributed around <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>19.7 billion to GDP in 2019. In 2018, Indonesia received 15.8Â million visitors, a growth of 12.5% from last year, and received an average receipt of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[209]</a></sup> China, Singapore, Malaysia, Australia, and Japan are the top five sources of visitors to Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[210]</a></sup> Since 2011, <i>Wonderful Indonesia</i> has been the country's international marketing campaign slogan to promote tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raja_Ampat_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/220px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/330px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Raja_Ampat_2.jpg/440px-Raja_Ampat_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raja_Ampat_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Raja_Ampat_Islands" title="Raja Ampat Islands">Raja Ampat Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Papua_(province)" title="West Papua (province)">West Papua</a>, has the highest recorded level of diversity in marine life, according to <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[212]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Nature and culture are prime attractions of Indonesian tourism. The country has a well-preserved natural ecosystem with rainforests stretching over about 57% of Indonesia's land (225Â million acres). Forests on Sumatra and Kalimantan are examples of popular destinations, such as the Orangutan wildlife reserve. Moreover, Indonesia has one of the world's longest coastlines, measuring 54,716 kilometres (33,999Â mi). The ancient <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prambanan" title="Prambanan">Prambanan</a> temples, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Toraja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> with their traditional festivities, are some of the popular destinations for cultural tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pariwisata_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-pariwisata-216">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Indonesia" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Indonesia">nine UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Komodo_National_Park" title="Komodo National Park">Komodo National Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ombilin_Coal_Mine" title="Ombilin Coal Mine">Sawahlunto Coal Mine</a>; and a further 19 in a tentative list that includes <a href="/wiki/Bunaken_National_Park" title="Bunaken National Park">Bunaken National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raja_Ampat_Islands" title="Raja Ampat Islands">Raja Ampat Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[214]</a></sup> Other attractions include specific points in Indonesian history, such as the colonial heritage of the Dutch East Indies in the <a href="/wiki/Old_town" title="Old town">old towns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kota_Tua_Jakarta" title="Kota Tua Jakarta">Jakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_architecture_in_Semarang" title="Dutch architecture in Semarang">Semarang</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_palaces_in_Indonesia" title="List of palaces in Indonesia">royal palaces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pagaruyung_Palace" title="Pagaruyung Palace">Pagaruyung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubud_Palace" title="Ubud Palace">Ubud</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kraton_Ngayogyakarta_Hadiningrat" title="Kraton Ngayogyakarta Hadiningrat">Yogyakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pariwisata_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-pariwisata-216">[213]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Indonesia" title="Demographics of Indonesia">Demographics of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesians" title="Indonesians">Indonesians</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_cities_by_population" title="List of Indonesian cities by population">List of Indonesian cities by population</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Indonesia" title="List of metropolitan areas in Indonesia">List of metropolitan areas in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Indonesien_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Indonesian_census" title="2020 Indonesian census">2020 census</a> recorded <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Indonesia" title="Demographics of Indonesia">Indonesia's population</a> as 270.2Â million, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">fourth largest in the world</a>, with a moderately high population growth rate of 1.25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> is the world's most populous island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[216]</a></sup> where 56% of the country's population lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020census_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-2020census-8">[8]</a></sup> The population density is 141 people per km<sup>2</sup> (365 per sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020census_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-2020census-8">[8]</a></sup> ranking 88th in the world, although Java has a population density of 1,067 people per km<sup>2</sup> (2,435 per sq mi). In 1961, the first post-colonial census recorded a total of 97Â million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[217]</a></sup> It is expected to grow to around 295Â million by 2030 and 321Â million by 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[218]</a></sup> The country currently possesses a relatively young population, with a median age of 30.2 years (2017 estimate).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-81">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>The spread of the population is uneven throughout the archipelago, with a varying habitats and levels of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indonesian_provinces_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of Indonesian provinces by Human Development Index">development</a>, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> of Jakarta to <a href="/wiki/Uncontacted_peoples" title="Uncontacted peoples">uncontacted tribes</a> in Papua.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[219]</a></sup> As of 2017, about 54.7% of the population lives in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[220]</a></sup> Jakarta is the country's <a href="/wiki/Primate_city" title="Primate city">primate city</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities" title="List of largest cities">second-most populous urban area globally</a>, with over 34Â million residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[221]</a></sup> About 8Â million <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Indonesians" title="Overseas Indonesians">Indonesians live overseas</a>; most settled in Malaysia, the Netherlands, Saudi Arabia, Taiwan, South Africa, Singapore, Hong Kong, the United States, and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[222]</a></sup>
</p>
