<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups_and_languages">Ethnic groups and languages</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">Ethnic groups in Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Native_Indonesians" title="Native Indonesians">Native Indonesians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">Languages of Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="215" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/330px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/495px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg/660px-Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesia_Ethnic_Groups_Map_English.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of ethnic groups in Indonesia</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesia is an ethnically diverse country, with around 1,300 distinct native ethnic groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPS_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> Most Indonesians are descended from <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a> whose languages had origins in <a href="/wiki/Proto-Austronesian_language" title="Proto-Austronesian language">Proto-Austronesian</a>, which possibly originated in what is now <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Another major grouping is the <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesians</a>, who inhabit eastern Indonesia (the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a> and the eastern part of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Sunda_Islands" title="Lesser Sunda Islands">Lesser Sunda Islands</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor20035â7_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor20035â7-27">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWitton2003139,_181,_251,_435_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWitton2003139,_181,_251,_435-226">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> are the largest ethnic group, constituting 40.2% of the population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPS_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> and are politically dominant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup> They are predominantly located in the central to eastern parts of Java and also in sizeable numbers in most provinces. The <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> are the next largest group (15.4%), followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_people" title="Batak people">Batak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madurese_people" title="Madurese people">Madurese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betawi_people" title="Betawi people">Betawi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bugis_people" title="Bugis people">Buginese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malay_Indonesians" title="Malay Indonesians">Malay</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[d]</a></sup> A sense of Indonesian nationhood exists alongside strong regional identities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991256_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs1991256-231">[227]</a></sup>
</p><p>The country's official language is <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, a variant of <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> based on its <a href="/wiki/Prestige_(sociolinguistics)" title="Prestige (sociolinguistics)">prestige dialect</a>, which had been the archipelago's <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> for centuries. It was <a href="/wiki/Youth_Pledge" title="Youth Pledge">promoted by nationalists in the 1920s</a> and achieved official status in 1945 under the name <i>Bahasa Indonesia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[228]</a></sup> Due to centuries-long contact with other languages, it is rich in local and foreign influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[e]</a></sup> Nearly every Indonesian speaks the language due to its widespread use in education, academics, communications, business, politics, and mass media. Most Indonesians also speak at least one of more than 700 local languages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup> often as their first language. Most belong to the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian language family</a>, while over 270 <a href="/wiki/Papuan_languages" title="Papuan languages">Papuan languages</a> are spoken in eastern Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup> Of these, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> is the most widely spoken<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-81">[79]</a></sup> and has co-official status in the <a href="/wiki/Special_Region_of_Yogyakarta" title="Special Region of Yogyakarta">Special Region of Yogyakarta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[232]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1930, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and other Europeans (<i><a href="/wiki/Totok" title="Totok">Totok</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Eurasians</a>, and derivative people like the <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indos</a>, numbered 240,000 or 0.4% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[233]</a></sup> Historically, they constituted only a tiny fraction of the native population and remain so today. Also, the Dutch language never had a substantial number of speakers or official status despite the Dutch presence for almost 350 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaker1998202_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaker1998202-239">[234]</a></sup> The small minorities that can speak it or <a href="/wiki/Dutch-based_creole_languages" title="Dutch-based creole languages">Dutch-based creole languages</a> fluently are the aforementioned ethnic groups and descendants of Dutch colonisers. This reflected the Dutch colonial empire's primary purpose, which was commercial exchange as opposed to sovereignty over homogeneous landmasses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ward_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ward-240">[235]</a></sup> Today, there is some degree of fluency by either educated members of the oldest generation or legal professionals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmmon20052017_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmmon20052017-241">[236]</a></sup> as specific law codes are still only available in Dutch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBooij19992_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBooij19992-242">[237]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Religion in Indonesia">Religion in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>Despite guaranteeing religious freedom in the constitution,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UUD45_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-UUD45-125">[123]</a></sup> the government officially recognises only <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Religion in Indonesia">six religions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Indonesia" title="Protestantism in Indonesia">Protestantism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Indonesia" title="Roman Catholicism in Indonesia">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Indonesia" title="Buddhism in Indonesia">Buddhism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_for_the_Confucian_Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Supreme Council for the Confucian Religion in Indonesia">Confucianism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-245">[240]</a></sup> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_religions" title="Indigenous religions">indigenous religions</a> only partly acknowledged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_245-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-245">[240]</a></sup> With 231 million adherents (86.7%) in 2018, Indonesia is the world's most populous Muslim-majority country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs2001379_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs2001379-246">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[242]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunnis</a> being the majority (99%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[243]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Shia Islam in Indonesia">Shias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_in_Indonesia" title="Ahmadiyya in Indonesia">Ahmadis</a>, respectively, constitute 1% (1â3Â million) and 0.2% (200,000â400,000) of Muslims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_245-2"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-245">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[244]</a></sup> Almost 11% of Indonesians are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, who form the <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Indonesia" title="Christianity in Indonesia">majority in seven provinces</a> in eastern Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[f]</a></sup> Most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> are <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[246]</a></sup> and most <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a> are <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesians" title="Chinese Indonesians">Chinese Indonesians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[247]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2809" data-file-width="4096" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg/220px-Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg/330px-Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg/440px-Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salah_Satu_Upacara_Besar_Di_Pura_Agung_Besakih.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> prayer ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Besakih_Temple" title="Besakih Temple">Besakih Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, the only Indonesian province where <a href="/wiki/Balinese_Hinduism" title="Balinese Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the predominant religion.</div></div></div>
<p>The natives of the Indonesian archipelago originally practised indigenous <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dynamism_(metaphysics)" title="Dynamism (metaphysics)">dynamism</a>, beliefs that are common to <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ooi_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi-254">[248]</a></sup> They worshipped and revered ancestral spirit and believed that supernatural spirits (<i><a href="/wiki/Hyang" title="Hyang">hyang</a></i>) might inhabit certain places such as large trees, stones, forests, mountains, or sacred sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ooi_254-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ooi-254">[248]</a></sup> Examples of Indonesian native belief systems include the <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Wiwitan" title="Sunda Wiwitan">Sunda Wiwitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Kaharingan" title="Kaharingan">Kaharingan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Kejaw%C3%A8n" title="KejawÃ¨n">KejawÃ¨n</a>. They have significantly impacted how other faiths are practised, evidenced by a large proportion of peopleâsuch as the Javanese <a href="/wiki/Abangan" title="Abangan">abangan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balinese_Hinduism" title="Balinese Hinduism">Balinese Hindus</a>, and Dayak Christiansâpractising a less <a href="/wiki/Orthodoxy" title="Orthodoxy">orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> form of their religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Indonesia" title="Hinduism in Indonesia">Hindu</a> influences reached the archipelago as early as the first century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[250]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdoms_of_Sunda" title="Kingdoms of Sunda">Kingdom</a> of <a href="/wiki/Salakanagara" title="Salakanagara">Salakanagara</a> in western Java around 130 was the first historically recorded <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Indianised</a> kingdom in the archipelago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[251]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Indonesia" title="Buddhism in Indonesia">Buddhism</a> arrived around the 6th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[252]</a></sup> and its history in Indonesia is closely related to that of Hinduism, as some empires based on Buddhism had their roots around the same period. The archipelago has witnessed the rise and fall of powerful and influential Hindu and Buddhist empires such as <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shailendra_dynasty" title="Shailendra dynasty">Sailendra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a>, and Mataram. Though no longer a majority, Hinduism and Buddhism remain to have a substantial influence on Indonesian culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque,_Indonesia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="284" data-file-width="394" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque%2C_Indonesia.jpg/220px-Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque%2C_Indonesia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque%2C_Indonesia.jpg/330px-Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque%2C_Indonesia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bd/Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque%2C_Indonesia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banda_Aceh%27s_Grand_Mosque,_Indonesia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Baiturrahman_Grand_Mosque" title="Baiturrahman Grand Mosque">Baiturrahman Grand Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Banda_Aceh" title="Banda Aceh">Banda Aceh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spread_of_Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Spread of Islam in Indonesia">spread of Islam in Indonesia</a> began in the region.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Islam in Indonesia">Islam</a> was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> traders of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shafi%27i" title="Shafi'i">Shafi'i</a> <a href="/wiki/Madhhab" title="Madhhab">school</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> traders from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Arabia" title="South Arabia">southern Arabia</a> as early as the 8th century CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[255]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[256]</a></sup> For the most part, Islam overlaid and mixed with existing cultural and religious influences, resulting in a distinct form of Islam (<i><a href="/wiki/Pesantren" title="Pesantren">santri</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112â14_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199112â14-36">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[257]</a></sup> Trade, <a href="/wiki/Islamic_missionary_activity" title="Islamic missionary activity">Islamic missionary activity</a> such as by the <a href="/wiki/Wali_Sanga" title="Wali Sanga">Wali Sanga</a> and Chinese explorer <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a>, and military campaigns by <a href="/wiki/Sultan#Southeast_and_East_Asia" title="Sultan">several sultanates</a> helped accelerate the <a href="/wiki/Spread_of_Islam_in_Indonesia" title="Spread of Islam in Indonesia">spread of Islam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[259]</a></sup> By the end of the 16th century, it had supplanted Hinduism and Buddhism as the dominant religion of <a href="/wiki/Java#Religion" title="Java">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra#Religion" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/220px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/330px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg/440px-Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_Cathedral_During_Mass.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Mary_of_the_Assumption_Cathedral,_Jakarta" title="St. Mary of the Assumption Cathedral, Jakarta">Jakarta Cathedral</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Indonesia" title="Catholic Church in Indonesia">Catholicism</a> was brought by Portuguese traders and missionaries such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> <a href="/wiki/Francis_Xavier" title="Francis Xavier">Francis Xavier</a>, who visited and baptised several thousand locals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199125,_26,_28_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199125,_26,_28-266">[260]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[261]</a></sup> Its spread faced difficulty due to the Dutch East India Company policy of banning the religion and the Dutch hostility due to the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> against Catholic Spain's rule. <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Indonesia" title="Protestantism in Indonesia">Protestantism</a> is mostly a result of <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> missionary efforts during the Dutch colonial era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERicklefs199128,_62_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERicklefs199128,_62-268">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVickers200522_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVickers200522-269">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[264]</a></sup> Although they are the most common branch, there is a multitude of other denominations elsewhere in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[265]</a></sup>
</p><p>There was a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Indonesia" title="History of the Jews in Indonesia">sizeable Jewish presence in the archipelago</a> until 1945, mostly Dutch and some Baghdadi Jews. Since most left after Indonesia proclaimed independence, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> was never accorded official status, and only a tiny number of Jews remain today, mostly in Jakarta and Surabaya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the national and local level, Indonesia's political leadership and civil society groups have played a crucial role in interfaith relations, both positively and negatively. The invocation of the first principle of Indonesia's philosophical foundation, Pancasila (i.e. the belief in the one and only God), often serves as a reminder of religious tolerance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[267]</a></sup> though instances of intolerance have occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIP_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIP-77">[75]</a></sup> An overwhelming majority of Indonesians consider religion to be essential and an integral part of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[269]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_health">Education and health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Indonesia" title="Education in Indonesia">Education in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Indonesia" title="Health in Indonesia">Health in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ITB_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/220px-ITB_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/330px-ITB_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/ITB_1.jpg/440px-ITB_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ITB_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bandung_Institute_of_Technology" title="Bandung Institute of Technology">Bandung Institute of Technology</a> in West Java</div></div></div>
<p>Education is compulsory for 12 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[270]</a></sup> Parents can choose between state-run, non-sectarian schools or private or semi-private religious (usually Islamic) schools, supervised by the ministries of Education and Religion, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[271]</a></sup> Private international schools that do not follow the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Indonesia#2013_curriculum" title="Education in Indonesia">national curriculum</a> are also available. The enrolment rate is 93% for primary education, 79% for secondary education, and 36% for tertiary education (2018).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UIS_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-UIS-278">[272]</a></sup> The literacy rate is 96% (2018), and the government spends about 3.6% of GDP (2015) on education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UIS_278-1"><a href="#cite_note-UIS-278">[272]</a></sup> In 2018, there were 4,670 higher educational institutions in Indonesia, with most (74%) located in Sumatra and Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[274]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>, Indonesia's top universities are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Indonesia" title="University of Indonesia">University of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gadjah_Mada_University" title="Gadjah Mada University">Gadjah Mada University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Institute_of_Technology" title="Bandung Institute of Technology">Bandung Institute of Technology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[275]</a></sup>
</p><p>Government expenditure on healthcare was about 3.3% of GDP in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[276]</a></sup> As part of an attempt to achieve universal health care, the government launched the National Health Insurance (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaminan_Kesehatan_Nasional" title="Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional">Jaminan Kesehatan Nasional</a></i>, JKN) in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[277]</a></sup> It includes coverage for a range of services from the public and also private firms that have opted to join the scheme. Despite remarkable improvements in recent decades, such as rising life expectancy (from 62.3 years in 1990 to 71.7 years in 2019)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[278]</a></sup> and declining child mortality (from 84 deaths per 1,000 births in 1990 to 23.9 deaths in 2019),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[279]</a></sup> challenges remain, including maternal and child health, low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>, high rate of <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">smoking</a>, and infectious diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[280]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Indonesia" title="Human rights in Indonesia">Human rights in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg/220px-Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg/330px-Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg/440px-Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jakarta_riot_14_May_1998.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Riots on the streets of Jakarta on 14 May 1998.</div></div></div>
<p>In the economic sphere, there is a gap in wealth, unemployment rate, and health between densely populated islands and economic centres (such as <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>) and sparsely populated, disadvantaged areas (such as <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Papua</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[281]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[282]</a></sup> This is created by a situation in which nearly 80% of Indonesia's population lives in the western parts of the archipelago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[283]</a></sup> and yet grows slower than the rest of the country.
</p><p>In the social arena, numerous cases of racism and discrimination, especially <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_Chinese_Indonesians" title="Discrimination against Chinese Indonesians">against Chinese Indonesians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people_of_New_Guinea" title="Indigenous people of New Guinea">Papuans</a>, have been well documented throughout Indonesia's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[284]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[285]</a></sup> Such cases have sometimes led to violent conflicts, most notably the <a href="/wiki/May_1998_riots_of_Indonesia" title="May 1998 riots of Indonesia">May 1998 riots</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>, which has continued since 1962. LGBT people also regularly face challenges. Although <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Indonesia" title="LGBT rights in Indonesia">LGBT issues</a> have been relatively obscure, the 2010s (especially after 2016) has seen a rapid surge of anti-LGBT rhetoric, putting LGBT Indonesians into a frequent subject of intimidation, discrimination, and even violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[286]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[287]</a></sup> In addition, Indonesia has been reported to have sizeable numbers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor">child</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" title="Forced labour">forced labourers</a>, with the former being prevalent in the palm oil and tobacco industries, while the latter in the fishing industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[288]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[289]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Indonesia" title="Culture of Indonesia">Culture of Indonesia</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/National_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_of_Indonesia" title="National Intangible Cultural Heritage of Indonesia">National Intangible Cultural Heritage of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Indonesia" title="Public holidays in Indonesia">Public holidays in Indonesia</a></div>
<p>The cultural history of the Indonesian archipelago spans more than two millennia. Influences from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JForshee_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-JForshee-296">[290]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[291]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a> have historically shaped the cultural, linguistic and religious makeup of the archipelago. As a result, modern-day Indonesia has a multicultural, multilingual and multi-ethnic society,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPS_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-BPS-4">[4]</a></sup> with a complex cultural mixture that differs significantly from the original indigenous cultures. Indonesia currently holds <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">twelve items of UNESCO's Intangible Cultural Heritage</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">wayang</a> puppet theatre, <a href="/wiki/Kris" title="Kris">kris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pencak_silat" title="Pencak silat">pencak silat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">angklung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a>, and the three genres of traditional <a href="/wiki/Balinese_dance" title="Balinese dance">Balinese dance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[293]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_art" title="Indonesian art">Indonesian art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Indonesia" title="Architecture of Indonesia">Architecture of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_painting" title="Indonesian painting">Indonesian painting</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="726" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/220px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/330px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg/440px-Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balinese_Cockfighting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Balinese painting depicting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cockfighting" title="Cockfighting">cockfighting</a></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesian arts include both age-old art forms developed through centuries and recently developed <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>. Despite often displaying local ingenuity, Indonesian arts have absorbed foreign influencesâmost notably from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, due to contacts and interactions facilitated, and often motivated by trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[294]</a></sup> Painting is an <a href="/wiki/Balinese_art" title="Balinese art">established and developed art in Bali</a>, where its people are famed for their artistry. Their painting tradition started as classical <a href="/wiki/Kamasan" title="Kamasan">Kamasan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a> style visual narrative, derived from visual art discovered on <i><a href="/wiki/Candi_of_Indonesia" title="Candi of Indonesia">candi</a></i> bas reliefs in eastern Java.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[295]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/220px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/330px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG/440px-Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Toraja_House.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An avenue of <a href="/wiki/Tongkonan" title="Tongkonan">Tongkonan</a> houses in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Torajan</a> village, <a href="/wiki/South_Sulawesi" title="South Sulawesi">South Sulawesi</a></div></div></div>
<p>There have been numerous discoveries of <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_art" title="Megalithic art">megalithic sculptures</a> in Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[296]</a></sup> Subsequently, tribal art has flourished within the culture of <a href="/wiki/Nias_people" title="Nias people">Nias</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batak_people" title="Batak people">Batak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asmat_people" title="Asmat people">Asmat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Toraja</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[297]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[298]</a></sup> Wood and stone are common materials used as the media for sculpting among these tribes. Between the 8th and 15th centuries, the Javanese civilisation developed refined stone sculpting art and architecture influenced by the Hindu-Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Dharma" title="Dharma">Dharmic</a> civilisation. The temples of <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prambanan" title="Prambanan">Prambanan</a> are among the most famous examples of the practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[299]</a></sup>
</p><p>As with the arts, Indonesian architecture has absorbed foreign influences that have brought cultural changes and profound effects on building styles and techniques. The most dominant has traditionally been <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_India" title="Architecture of India">Indian</a>; however, Chinese, Arab, and European influences have also been significant. Traditional carpentry, masonry, stone and woodwork techniques and decorations have thrived in <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_architecture" title="Vernacular architecture">vernacular architecture</a>, with numbers of traditional houses' (<i><a href="/wiki/Rumah_adat" title="Rumah adat">rumah adat</a></i>) styles that have been developed. The traditional houses and settlements vary by ethnic group, and each has a specific custom and history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[300]</a></sup> Examples include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toraja" title="Toraja">Toraja</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tongkonan" title="Tongkonan">Tongkonan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Rumah_Gadang" title="Rumah Gadang">Rumah Gadang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangkiang" title="Rangkiang">Rangkiang</a>, Javanese style <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pendopo" title="Pendopo">Pendopo</a> pavilion with <a href="/wiki/Joglo" title="Joglo">Joglo</a> style roof, <a href="/wiki/Dayak_people" title="Dayak people">Dayak</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Longhouse" title="Longhouse">longhouses</a>, various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rumah_Melayu" title="Rumah Melayu">Malay houses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balinese_architecture" title="Balinese architecture">Balinese houses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balinese_temple" title="Balinese temple">temples</a>, and also different forms of <a href="/wiki/Rice_barn" title="Rice barn">rice barns</a> (<i>lumbung</i>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Music.2C_dance_and_clothing"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Music,_dance_and_clothing">Music, dance and clothing</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Indonesia" title="Music of Indonesia">Music of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Indonesia" title="Dance in Indonesia">Dance in Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_costume_of_Indonesia" title="National costume of Indonesia">National costume of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:169px;max-width:169px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" width="146"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:140px;max-width:140px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:97px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/138px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/207px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg/276px-Jaipongan_Bunga_Tanjung_02.jpg 2x" width="138"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Indonesian music and dance. Clockwise from top: A <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a> player, <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a>, Sundanese <a href="/wiki/Jaipongan" title="Jaipongan">Jaipongan</a> Mojang Priangan dance, Balinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pendet" title="Pendet">Pendet</a> dance.</div></div></div></div>
<p>The music of Indonesia predates historical records. Various indigenous tribes incorporate chants and songs accompanied by musical instruments in their rituals. <a href="/wiki/Angklung" title="Angklung">Angklung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kacapi_suling" title="Kacapi suling">kacapi suling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gong" title="Gong">gong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talempong" title="Talempong">talempong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kulintang" title="Kulintang">kulintang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sasando" title="Sasando">sasando</a> are examples of traditional Indonesian instruments. The diverse world of Indonesian music genres results from the musical creativity of its people and subsequent cultural encounters with foreign influences. These include <a href="/wiki/Qanb%C5%ABs" title="QanbÅ«s">gambus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qasida" title="Qasida">qasida</a> from the Middle East,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[301]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keroncong" title="Keroncong">keroncong</a> from Portugal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[302]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dangdut" title="Dangdut">dangdut</a>âone of Indonesia's most popular music genresâwith notable Hindi influence as well as Malay orchestras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[303]</a></sup> Today, the Indonesian music industry enjoys both nationwide and regional popularity in Malaysia, Singapore, and Brunei,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[304]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[305]</a></sup> due to the common culture and <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_Indonesian_and_Standard_Malay" title="Comparison of Indonesian and Standard Malay">mutual intelligibility</a> between <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[306]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="501" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/170px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/255px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg/340px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Katoenen_wikkelrok_met_geometrisch_patroon_TMnr_5713-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Indonesian <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a></div></div></div>
<p>Indonesian dances have a diverse history, with more than 3,000 original dances. Scholars believe that they had their beginning in rituals and religious worship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[307]</a></sup> Examples include war dances, a dance of <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctors</a>, and a dance to call for rain or any agricultural rituals such as <a href="/wiki/Hudoq" title="Hudoq">Hudoq</a>. Indonesian dances derive their influences from the archipelago's prehistoric and tribal, Hindu-Buddhist, and Islamic periods. Recently, modern dances and urban teen dances have gained popularity due to the influence of Western culture and those of Japan and South Korea to some extent. However, various traditional dances, including those of Java, Bali and Dayak, remain a living and dynamic tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[308]</a></sup>
</p><p>Indonesia has various clothing styles due to its long and rich cultural history. The national costume originates from the country's indigenous culture and traditional textile traditions. The Javanese <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">Batik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kebaya" title="Kebaya">Kebaya</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[309]</a></sup> are arguably Indonesia's most recognised national costumes, though they have <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a> origins as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-316">[310]</a></sup> Each province has a representation of traditional attire and dress,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JForshee_296-1"><a href="#cite_note-JForshee-296">[290]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Ulos" title="Ulos">Ulos</a> of <a href="/wiki/Batak" title="Batak">Batak</a> from <a href="/wiki/North_Sumatra" title="North Sumatra">North Sumatra</a>; <a href="/wiki/Songket" title="Songket">Songket</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a> from Sumatra; and <a href="/wiki/Ikat" title="Ikat">Ikat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sasak_people" title="Sasak people">Sasak</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a>. People wear national and regional costumes during traditional weddings, formal ceremonies, music performances, government and official occasions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_316-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-316">[310]</a></sup> and they vary from traditional to modern attire.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_cinema">Theatre and cinema</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Indonesia" title="Theatre of Indonesia">Theatre of Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Indonesia" title="Cinema of Indonesia">Cinema of Indonesia</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Indonesia" title="List of highest-grossing films in Indonesia">List of highest-grossing films in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1261" data-file-width="2268" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/220px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/330px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg/440px-Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Wong_Bharata_Pandawa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pandava" title="Pandava">Pandava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krishna" title="Krishna">Krishna</a> in an act of the <i>Wayang Wong</i> performance</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">Wayang</a>, the Javanese, Sundanese, and Balinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shadow_puppet" title="Shadow puppet">shadow puppet</a> theatre display several mythological legends such as <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[311]</a></sup> Other forms of local drama include the Javanese <a href="/wiki/Ludruk" title="Ludruk">Ludruk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ketoprak" title="Ketoprak">Ketoprak</a>, the Sundanese <a href="/wiki/Sandiwara" title="Sandiwara">Sandiwara</a>, Betawi <a href="/wiki/Lenong" title="Lenong">Lenong</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[313]</a></sup> and various Balinese dance dramas. They incorporate humour and jest and often involve audiences in their performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[314]</a></sup> Some theatre traditions also include music, dancing and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" title="Pencak Silat">silat</a> martial art, such as <a href="/wiki/Randai" title="Randai">Randai</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau people</a> of West Sumatra. It is usually performed for traditional ceremonies and festivals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-randai_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-randai-322">[316]</a></sup> and based on semi-historical Minangkabau legends and love story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-randai_322-1"><a href="#cite_note-randai-322">[316]</a></sup> Modern performing art also developed in Indonesia with its distinct style of drama. Notable theatre, dance, and drama troupe such as <i>Teater Koma</i> are famous as it often portrays social and political satire of Indonesian society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[317]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2040" data-file-width="1592" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/170px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/255px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg/340px-Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Loetoeng_Kasaroeng_p67.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Advertisement for <i><a href="/wiki/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng" title="Loetoeng Kasaroeng">Loetoeng Kasaroeng</a></i> (1926), the first fiction film produced in the Dutch East Indies</div></div></div>
<p>The first film produced in the archipelago was <i><a href="/wiki/Loetoeng_Kasaroeng" title="Loetoeng Kasaroeng">Loetoeng Kasaroeng</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctrip_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ctrip-324">[318]</a></sup> a silent film by Dutch director L. Heuveldorp. The film industry expanded after independence, with six films made in 1949 rising to 58 in 1955. <a href="/wiki/Usmar_Ismail" title="Usmar Ismail">Usmar Ismail</a>, who made significant imprints in the 1950s and 1960s, is generally considered the pioneer of Indonesian films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[319]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guided_Democracy_in_Indonesia" title="Guided Democracy in Indonesia">latter part of the Sukarno era</a> saw the use of cinema for nationalistic, anti-Western purposes, and foreign films were subsequently banned, while the New Order utilised a censorship code that aimed to maintain social order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krishna_Sen_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krishna_Sen-326">[320]</a></sup> Production of films peaked during the 1980s, although it declined significantly in the next decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ctrip_324-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ctrip-324">[318]</a></sup> Notable films in this period include <i><a href="/wiki/Satan%27s_Slave_(1980_film)" title="Satan's Slave (1980 film)">Pengabdi Setan</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/Nagabonar" title="Nagabonar">Nagabonar</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/Tjoet_Nja%27_Dhien" title="Tjoet Nja' Dhien">Tjoet Nja' Dhien</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Catatan_Si_Boy" title="Catatan Si Boy">Catatan Si Boy</a></i> (1989), and <a href="/wiki/Warkop" title="Warkop">Warkop</a>'s comedy films.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">Independent filmmaking</a> was a rebirth of the film industry since 1998, when films started addressing previously banned topics, such as religion, race, and love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krishna_Sen_326-1"><a href="#cite_note-Krishna_Sen-326">[320]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2005, the number of films released each year steadily increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[321]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Riri_Riza" title="Riri Riza">Riri Riza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mira_Lesmana" title="Mira Lesmana">Mira Lesmana</a> were among the new generation of filmmakers who co-directed <i>Kuldesak</i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Petualangan_Sherina" title="Petualangan Sherina">Petualangan Sherina</a></i> (2000), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ada_Apa_dengan_Cinta%3F" title="Ada Apa dengan Cinta?">Ada Apa dengan Cinta?</a></i> (2002), and <i><a href="/wiki/Laskar_Pelangi" title="Laskar Pelangi">Laskar Pelangi</a></i> (2008). In 2016, <i>Warkop DKI Reborn: Jangkrik Boss Part 1</i> smashed box office records, becoming the most-watched Indonesian film with 6.8Â million tickets sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[322]</a></sup> Indonesia has held annual film festivals and awards, including the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Film_Festival" title="Indonesian Film Festival">Indonesian Film Festival</a> (<i>Festival Film Indonesia</i>) held intermittently since 1955. It hands out the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citra_Award" title="Citra Award">Citra Award</a>, the film industry's most prestigious award. From 1973 to 1992, the festival was held annually and then discontinued until its revival in 2004.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_media_and_literature">Mass media and literature</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mass_media_in_Indonesia" title="Mass media in Indonesia">Mass media in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_literature" title="Indonesian literature">Indonesian literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium,_Jakarta,_MetroTV.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1748" data-file-width="2551" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/220px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/330px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg/440px-TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium%2C_Jakarta%2C_MetroTV.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TV_News_Media_in_GBK_Stadium,_Jakarta,_MetroTV.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Metro_TV_(Indonesian_TV_network)" title="Metro TV (Indonesian TV network)">Metro TV</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gelora_Bung_Karno_Stadium" title="Gelora Bung Karno Stadium">Gelora Bung Karno Stadium</a>, reporting the <a href="/wiki/2010_AFF_Championship" title="2010 AFF Championship">2010 AFF Championship</a></div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_Indonesia" title="Media of Indonesia">Media</a> freedom increased considerably after the fall of the New Order, during which the Ministry of Information monitored and controlled domestic media and restricted foreign media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[323]</a></sup> The television market includes several national commercial networks and provincial networks that compete with public <a href="/wiki/TVRI" title="TVRI">TVRI</a>, which held a monopoly on TV broadcasting from 1962 to 1989. By the early 21st century, the improved communications system had brought television signals to every village, and people can choose from up to 11 channels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frd2011_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-frd2011-330">[324]</a></sup> Private radio stations carry news bulletins while foreign broadcasters supply programmes. The number of printed publications has increased significantly since 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frd2011_330-1"><a href="#cite_note-frd2011-330">[324]</a></sup>
</p><p>Like other developing countries, Indonesia began developing <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> in the early 1990s. Its first commercial <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a>, PT. Indo Internet began operation in Jakarta in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[325]</a></sup> The country had 171Â million Internet users in 2018, with a penetration rate that keeps increasing annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[326]</a></sup> Most are between the ages of 15 and 19 and depend primarily on mobile phones for access, outnumbering laptops and computers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[327]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1234" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/170px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/255px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg/340px-Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pramudya_Ananta_Tur_Kesusastraan_Modern_Indonesia_p226.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pramoedya_Ananta_Toer" title="Pramoedya Ananta Toer">Pramoedya Ananta Toer</a>, Indonesia's most famous novelist. Many considered him to be Southeast Asia's leading candidate for a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[328]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The oldest evidence of writing in the Indonesian archipelago is a series of <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> inscriptions dated to the 5th century. Many of Indonesia's peoples have firmly rooted <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral traditions</a>, which help define and preserve their cultural identities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[329]</a></sup> In written poetry and prose, several traditional forms dominate, mainly <a href="/wiki/Syair" title="Syair">syair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantun" title="Pantun">pantun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurindam" title="Gurindam">gurindam</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Hikayat" title="List of Hikayat">hikayat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_historical_texts" title="Javanese historical texts">babad</a>. Examples of these forms include <i><a href="/wiki/Syair_Abdul_Muluk" title="Syair Abdul Muluk">Syair Abdul Muluk</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hikayat_Hang_Tuah" title="Hikayat Hang Tuah">Hikayat Hang Tuah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Malay_Annals" title="Malay Annals">Sulalatus Salatin</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Babad_Tanah_Jawi" title="Babad Tanah Jawi">Babad Tanah Jawi</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[330]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early modern Indonesian literature originates in the Sumatran tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[331]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[332]</a></sup> Literature and poetry flourished during the decades leading up to and after independence. <a href="/wiki/Balai_Pustaka" title="Balai Pustaka">Balai Pustaka</a>, the government bureau for popular literature, was instituted in 1917 to promote the development of indigenous literature. Many scholars consider the 1950s and 1960s to be the Golden Age of Indonesian Literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-literary_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-literary-339">[333]</a></sup> The style and characteristics of modern Indonesian literature vary according to the dynamics of the country's political and social landscape,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-literary_339-1"><a href="#cite_note-literary-339">[333]</a></sup> most notably the war of independence in the second half of the 1940s and the anti-communist mass killings in the mid-1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[334]</a></sup> Notable literary figures of the modern era include <a href="/wiki/Multatuli" title="Multatuli">Multatuli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chairil_Anwar" title="Chairil Anwar">Chairil Anwar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Yamin" title="Mohammad Yamin">Mohammad Yamin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merari_Siregar" title="Merari Siregar">Merari Siregar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marah_Roesli" title="Marah Roesli">Marah Roesli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pramoedya_Ananta_Toer" title="Pramoedya Ananta Toer">Pramoedya Ananta Toer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ayu_Utami" title="Ayu Utami">Ayu Utami</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_cuisine" title="Indonesian cuisine">Indonesian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1976" data-file-width="2635" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/220px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/330px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG/440px-Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nasi_ramas_rendang.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasi_Padang" title="Nasi Padang">Nasi Padang</a></i> with <i><a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gulai" title="Gulai">gulai</a></i> and vegetables</div></div></div>
<p>Indonesian cuisine is one of the world's most diverse, vibrant, and colourful, full of intense flavour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[335]</a></sup> Many regional cuisines exist, often based upon indigenous culture and foreign influences such as Chinese, European, Middle Eastern, and Indian precedents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[336]</a></sup> Rice is the leading <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple food</a> and is served with <a href="/wiki/Side_dish" title="Side dish">side dishes</a> of meat and vegetables. Spices (notably chilli), <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>, fish and chicken are fundamental ingredients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[337]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some popular dishes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">nasi goreng</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gado-gado" title="Gado-gado">gado-gado</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">sate</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Soto_(food)" title="Soto (food)">soto</a></i> are ubiquitous and considered national dishes. The Ministry of Tourism, however, chose <i><a href="/wiki/Tumpeng" title="Tumpeng">tumpeng</a></i> as the official national dish in 2014, describing it as binding the diversity of various culinary traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[338]</a></sup> Other popular dishes include <i><a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a></i>, one of the many <a href="/wiki/Padang_cuisine" title="Padang cuisine">Padang cuisines</a> along with <i><a href="/wiki/Dendeng" title="Dendeng">dendeng</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gulai" title="Gulai">gulai</a></i>. Another fermented food is <i><a href="/wiki/Oncom" title="Oncom">oncom</a></i>, similar in some ways to <i><a href="/wiki/Tempeh" title="Tempeh">tempeh</a></i> but uses a variety of bases (not only soy), created by different fungi, and is prevalent in <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[339]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Indonesia" title="Sport in Indonesia">Sport in Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_martial_arts" title="Indonesian martial arts">Indonesian martial arts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1518" data-file-width="1140" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg/170px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg/255px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg/340px-Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pencak_Silat_Betawi_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A demonstration of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" title="Pencak Silat">Pencak Silat</a></i>, a form of martial arts</div></div></div><p><a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">Badminton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> are the most popular sports in Indonesia. Indonesia is among the few countries that have won the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cup" title="Thomas Cup">Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uber_Cup" title="Uber Cup">Uber Cup</a>, the world team championship of men's and women's badminton. Along with <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a>, it is the sport that contributes the most to <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_at_the_Olympics" title="Indonesia at the Olympics">Indonesia's Olympic medal tally</a>. <a href="/wiki/Liga_1_(Indonesia)" title="Liga 1 (Indonesia)">Liga 1</a> is the country's premier football club league. On the international stage, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_national_football_team" title="Indonesia national football team">Indonesia</a> was the first Asian team to participate in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1938_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1938 FIFA World Cup">1938</a> as the Dutch East Indies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[340]</a></sup> On a regional level, Indonesia won a bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/1958_Asian_Games" title="1958 Asian Games">1958 Asian Games</a> as well as two gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/1987_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="1987 Southeast Asian Games">1987</a> and <a href="/wiki/1991_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="1991 Southeast Asian Games">1991 Southeast Asian Games</a> (SEA Games). Indonesia's first appearance at the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a> was in <a href="/wiki/1996_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1996 AFC Asian Cup">1996</a> and successfully qualified for a total of five tournaments, although they never make the knockout phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[341]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, which has a long history in Indonesia and was part of the first <a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Week_(Indonesia)" title="National Sports Week (Indonesia)">National Games</a> (<i>Pekan Olahraga Nasional</i>, PON) in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[342]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sepak_takraw" title="Sepak takraw">Sepak takraw</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Karapan_sapi" title="Karapan sapi">karapan sapi</a></i> (bull racing) in <a href="/wiki/Madura_Island" title="Madura Island">Madura</a> are some examples of Indonesia's traditional sports. In areas with a history of tribal warfare, mock fighting contests are held, such as <i>caci</i> in <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pasola" title="Pasola">pasola</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Sumba" title="Sumba">Sumba</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pencak_Silat" title="Pencak Silat">Pencak Silat</a></i> is an Indonesian martial art and, in 1987, became one of the sporting events in the SEA Games, with Indonesia appearing as one of the leading competitors. In Southeast Asia, Indonesia is one of the top sports powerhouses by topping the SEA Games medal table ten times since 1977,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[343]</a></sup> most recently in <a href="/wiki/2011_Southeast_Asian_Games" title="2011 Southeast Asian Games">2011</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[344]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-fn2-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn2_151-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="IndonesiaâMalaysia confrontation">IndonesiaâMalaysia confrontation</a>, Indonesia withdrew from the UN due to the latter's election to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, although it returned 18 months later. It marked the first time in UN history that a member state had attempted a withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-230"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-230">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Small but significant populations of <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">ethnic Chinese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indians</a>, Europeans and Arabs are concentrated mostly in urban areas.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-236">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These influences include Javanese, Sundanese, Minangkabau, Makassarese, Hindustani, Sanskrit, Tamil, Chinese, Arabic, Dutch, Portuguese and English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[231]</a></sup></span>
</li>
